## THE THE BURGESS BURGESS PERSIAN PERSIAN LETTERS LETTERS Edited Edited by by BENJAMIN BENJAMIN SCHWARTZ SCHWARTZ 

## PART PART Il II 

[Henry [HENRY Burcess BURGESS To TO CHARLES CHARLES BurcEss] BURGESS] Hempstead, Hempstead, October October 18, 18, 1830 1830 Mr. Mr. Hanson Hanson gave gave me me yesterday yesterday a a deplorable deplorable account account of of the the condition condition of of the the East East whither whither you you and and my my dear dear Edward Edward are are bending bending your your steps. steps. He He says says that that the the Plague Plague is is raging raging at at Trebizonde Trebizonde and and other other places: places :[—] — that that the the Cholera Cholera morbus morbus has has not not yet yet spent spent its its ravages: ravages : —[—] that that trade trade is is very very bad bad in in Persia, Persia, and and that that the the Persians Persians will will buy buy nothing nothing at at Constantinople. Constantinople. But, But, he he anticipated, anticipated, that that in in a a few few months months the the diseases diseases would would disappear disappear and and trade trade revive. revive. Tabreez, Tabreez, October October 12, 12, 1837 1837 Having Having heard heard that that some some skins[skins] of of birds birds sent sent to to England England from from the the neighbourneighbour hood hood of of Erzeroum Erzeroum and and Trebizonde Trebizonde have have bten been thought thought interesting interesting I I have have taken taken the the liberty liberty of of sending sending to to the the Society Society two two birds birds of of the the partridge partridge kind, kind, which, which, as as they they are[are] rare[rare] in[in] this[this] country, country, I I hope hope may may[not] not be[be] found[found] unworthy unworthy of[of] the[the] Societys Societys acceptance. acceptance.44 ** 

They They are are called called in in the[the] language language of of the[the] natives[natives] of of this[this] country, country, Turkish, Turkish, "vor “vdr keklik” keklik" and and in in Persian, Persian, “‘cafik "cafik i i ders,”” ders," which which may may be be translated translated “partridge "partridge of of the the wilderness.” wilderness." These These birds birds were were sent sent to to me me in in the the month month of of July July last last and and I I put put them them into into a a small small garden garden adjoining adjoining my my house house and and fed fed them them on on wheat wheat but but they they also also eat eat a a great great quantity quantity of the of the leaves leaves and and even even stalks stalks of of kidney kidney beans beans and and other other kitchen kitchen garden garden plants plants and[and] upon upon this[this] food[food] they they became[became] fat fat and and seemed seemed healthy. healthy. They They inhabit[inhabit] the the most most inaccessible inaccessible and and highest highest places places in in the the mountains mountains of of Persia, Persia, and and do do not not descend descend towards towards the the plains plains in in winter, winter, which which in in this this country country even even in in the the plains, plains, is is exceedingly exceedingly severe. severe. They They are are said said to to feed feed at at that that season, season, when when the the whole whole country country is is covered covered with with snow, snow, on on the the sides sides of of the the steepest steepest banks banks and and rocky rocky ravines ravines facing facing the the south, south, where where the the snow snow never never remains remains long long and and is is never never deep, deep, and and there there they they find find in in plenty plenty the the seeds seeds of of the the mountain mountain plants plants which which grow grow in in such such places, places, and and which which I I have have observed observed to to form form the the chief chief food food of of the the red legged red legged partridge, partridge, which which is is numerous numerous here. here.

If If I I had had been been free free from from my my embarrassments[embarrassments] on on Charles’ Charles' acct acct I I might might perhaps perhaps have have obtained obtained the the latter latter place. place. I I believe believe the the pay pay is is £350 £350 or or £400 £400 a a year year with with liberty liberty to to trade. trade. But But my my present present position position prevents prevents my my trying trying to to get get any any situation situation whatever. whatever. The The road road between between this this and and Erzeroum Erzeroum is is now now much much disturbed, disturbed, two two English English gentlemen gentlemen coming coming from from Constantinople Constantinople were were robbed robbed near near this this frontier frontier a a short short time time ago ago and and narrowly narrowly escaped escaped being being murdered,[murdered,] the the spears spears of of the the brigands brigands having having passed passed thro’ thro' their their clothes clothes and and slightly slightly wounded wounded them. them. When When the the robbers robbers (Koords) (Koords) found found they they were were English English they they gave gave them them back back the the most most part part of of their their clothes clothes but but took took all all their their money money and and valuables, valuables, and and their their servants servants were were stripped stripped to to their their shirts shirts and and drawers. drawers. Caravans Caravans now now go go a a good good many many together together so so as as to to form form a a large large party party and and there there is is no no more more danger danger to to merchandize merchandize than than formerly. formerly. But But many many single single travellers travellers and and small small parties parties have have been been robbed robbed and and some some people people murdered. murdered.

Last Last year[year] it it has has been been committing[committing] dreadful dreadful ravages ravages in in Afghanistan Afghanistan and and in in the the autumn autumn had had come come as as far far as as Meshed Meshed and and Nishahpoor[Nishahpoor] on on the the way[way] to to Tehran. There There were were five five or six six of them them in the the room room and and it would would have have amused amused you[you] to have have seen seen their their blanc blanc faces. faces. > Talking Talking of cholera cholera have have you[you] read read “‘the “the wandering[wandering] Jew” Jew” by Eugene Eugene Sue, Sue, I have have just just finished finished it (the (the translation translation in the the[“Family] “Family Herald” Herald”)” )*’ and and think think it a most most clever clever novel,[novel,] if you you have have not not read read it, it will will[please] please you[you] much much as its aim aim is to better better the the condition condition of the the[working] working classes,[classes,] and and unmask unmask the the villainy[villainy] of the the Jesuits. > My My husband husband applied applied himself himself with with knowledge knowledge to to the the Government Government business business. . But But he he was was always[always] sad sad about about his his brother, brother[,] and and for for his his dear dear father father and and mother mother so so far away. away Every Every time time he had had the the fever, fever more more pain pain settled settled in his his back back and and limbs. limbs Our Our[baby] baby was was then then delicate delicate in the the stomach, stomach and and was was always always sick. sick He He died died at eighteen eighteen months months old. old My My Edward Edward mourned mourned him him as if he he had had been been older, older for for he he had had 

> hoped hoped to send send him him to England, England to give give him him to his his dear dear father father to put put to school. school 

> We We buried buried his his body[body] in the the Armenian Armenian graveyard[graveyard] in Tehran. Tehran When When our our Fanny was[Fanny] was born, born we we saw saw that that she she too too was was something[something] like like her her father, father but but not not quite[quite] so much much 

> as our our boy[boy] was. was Edward Edward grew grew weaker, weaker and and more more often often ill, and and I worked worked, worked, worked for for him and and for for my[my] baby.[baby] I would would not not let him do anything anything I could could do for for him him. Then Then it was was said said “‘if he was was to live live at all, he must must be taken taken to England.” England We We let our our house house and and sold sold all we we could could for money money for for the the journey journey & to provide provide that that Charles’ Charles children children should should not not die die of want want of food, food for for he loved loved them them for for Charles’ Charles sake. sake The The Government Government gave[gave] him him six months months leave leave of absence, absence and and the the[money] money for for all that that time. time But But oh! our our hearts hearts did tremble tremble and and sink, sink for he grew grew thin thin as a skeleton. skeleton Mr. Mr Ronald Ronald Thompson Thompson and and the the doctor doctor got got for for him him a takhteravan takhteravan — a what what you[you] say, say a litter litter slung slung between between two two mules mules, to travel travel in. And And sometimes sometimes I rode rodeandmore and more often often I walked walked by his side. side The The servant servant had had our our Fanny[Fanny] on another another mule mule. It was was a very very dreadful dreadful journey. journey We We travelled travelled as fast fast as we we could, could for for he longed longed to see see his his own own country. country Often Often we we were were obliged obliged to stay stay at those those very very dreadful dreadful Mahommedan Mahommedan villages, villages lest lest he should should die die with with the the hard hard travel: travel for for the the disease disease had had settled settled in his spine spine and and limbs, limbs and and often often movement movement gave gave him him such such agony agony that that he looked looked as dead. dead I never never left left him, he was was in my my eyes eyes night night and and day day. I cooked cooked for him and and washed washed by the the road-side. road side My My life life was was in his his life: life I saw saw not not our our baby,[baby] I saw saw not not anything[anything] but but[my] my husband. husband Our Our money,[money] and and our our pro[pro] visions visions for for the the road road were were using[using] up — Oh! we we were were nearly[nearly] three three months months on that that journey journey from from Tehran Tehràn to Tabriz! Tabriz When When we we were were eight eight days days from from Tabriz, Tabriz there there came came to meet meet us my my father, father my my two two uncles, uncles and and[my] my kind kind brother, brother Dr. Dr Cormick. Cormick Then Then I trusted trusted that that they[they] would would guide guide us safe. safe We We both both had had had had the the horrible horrible knowledge, knowledge that, that if he had had had had to be buried buried outside outside one one of those those villages,[villages] the the dogs dogs would would have have eaten eaten him him directly. directly But But we we reached reached Tabriz Tabriz after after eight eight days, days and and laid laid him him in his his own own house house, and and Dr. Cormick Cormick attended attended to him him.
